<p>"<b>...Baby One More Time</b>" is the debut single by American singer <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>. It was written and produced by <a href="/wiki/Max_Martin" title="Max Martin">Max Martin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rami_Yacoub" title="Rami Yacoub">Rami</a>, and released in 1998, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JIVE_Records" title="JIVE Records">JIVE Records</a> for Spears' <a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)" title="...Baby One More Time (album)">debut studio album of the same name</a> (1999). After recording and sending a demo tape with an unused song from <a href="/wiki/Toni_Braxton" title="Toni Braxton">Toni Braxton</a>, Spears signed a multi-album deal with JIVE. "...Baby One More Time" is a <a href="/wiki/Teen_pop" title="Teen pop">teen pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> song that refers to a girl's feelings after a break-up with her boyfriend. The song received generally favorable reviews from critics, who praised its composition.</p>
<p>"...Baby One More Time" reached number one in several countries, including the United Kingdom, where it earned double-platinum status and became the country's best-selling song of 1999. It is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles" title="List of best-selling singles">best-selling singles of all time</a>, with over 10 million copies sold. An accompanying music video, directed by <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Dick" title="Nigel Dick">Nigel Dick</a>, portrays Spears as a student from a Catholic high school, who starts to <a href="/wiki/Daydream" title="Daydream">daydream</a> that she is singing and dancing around the school, while watching her love interest from afar. The music video was later referenced in the music video of "<a href="/wiki/If_U_Seek_Amy" title="If U Seek Amy">If U Seek Amy</a>" (2008), where Spears's fictional daughter is dressed with a similar schoolgirl outfit while wearing pink ribbons in her hair. In 2010, the music video for "...Baby One More Time" was voted the third most influential video in the history of pop music, in a poll held by <a href="/wiki/Jam!" title="Jam!">Jam!</a>. In 2011, "...Baby One More Time" was voted the best music video of the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> It has been featured on all of her greatest hits and other compilation albums.</p>
<p>Spears has performed "...Baby One More Time" in a number of live appearances and in all of her concert tours. It was the encore of the <a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_Tour" title="...Baby One More Time Tour">...Baby One More Time Tour</a> (1999) and <a href="/wiki/Dream_Within_a_Dream_Tour" title="Dream Within a Dream Tour">Dream Within a Dream Tour</a> (2001); Spears also performed remixed versions of the song during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oops!..._I_Did_It_Again_World_Tour" title="Oops!... I Did It Again World Tour">Oops!... I Did It Again World Tour</a> (2000), <a href="/wiki/The_Onyx_Hotel_Tour" title="The Onyx Hotel Tour">The Onyx Hotel Tour</a> (2004), <a href="/wiki/The_M%2BM%27s_Tour" title="The M+M's Tour">The M+M's Tour</a> (2007), <a href="/wiki/The_Circus_Starring_Britney_Spears" title="The Circus Starring Britney Spears">The Circus Starring Britney Spears</a> (2009), the <a href="/wiki/Femme_Fatale_Tour" title="Femme Fatale Tour">Femme Fatale Tour</a> (2011), and <a href="/wiki/Britney:_Piece_of_Me" title="Britney: Piece of Me">Britney: Piece of Me</a> (2013). "...Baby One More Time" was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a>, and has been included in lists by <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>. It has been noted for redefining the sound of late 1990s music. Spears has named "...Baby One More Time" as one of her favorite songs from her career. It was also the final song to be played on the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>'s music programme <i><a href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops" title="Top of the Pops">Top of the Pops</a></i> in the 1990s.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<tr>
<td style="width:20px; vertical-align:top;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cquote1.png"><img alt="Cquote1.png" data-file-height="30" data-file-width="40" height="8" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Cquote1.png/10px-Cquote1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Cquote1.png/15px-Cquote1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Cquote1.png/20px-Cquote1.png 2x" width="10"/></a></td>
<td style="text-align:left;">
<p>I had been in studio for about six months listening and recording material, but I hadn't really heard a hit yet. When I started working with Max Martin in Sweden, he played the demo for 'Baby One More Time' for me, and I knew from the start it one was of those songs you want to hear again and again. It just felt really right. I went into the studio and did my own thing with it, trying to give it a little more attitude than the demo. In 10 days, I never even saw Sweden. We were so busy.</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="3">
<div style="text-align: right;">—Spears talking to Chuck Taylor of <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></div>
</td>
<td style="width:20px; vertical-align:top;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cquote2.png"><img alt="Cquote2.png" data-file-height="30" data-file-width="40" height="8" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Cquote2.png/10px-Cquote2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Cquote2.png/15px-Cquote2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Cquote2.png/20px-Cquote2.png 2x" width="10"/></a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In June 1997, Spears was in talks with manager <a href="/wiki/Lou_Pearlman" title="Lou Pearlman">Lou Pearlman</a> to join female pop group <a href="/wiki/Innosense" title="Innosense">Innosense</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes145_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-hughes145-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lynne_Spears" title="Lynne Spears">Lynne Spears</a> asked family friend and entertainment lawyer <a href="/wiki/Larry_Rudolph" title="Larry Rudolph">Larry Rudolph</a> for his opinion and submitted a tape of Spears singing over a <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a> karaoke song along with some pictures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes145_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-hughes145-4">[4]</a></sup> Rudolph decided he wanted to pitch her to record labels, therefore she needed a professional demo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes145_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-hughes145-4">[4]</a></sup> He sent Spears an unused song from <a href="/wiki/Toni_Braxton" title="Toni Braxton">Toni Braxton</a>; she rehearsed for a week and recorded her vocals in a studio with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audio_engineering" title="Audio engineering">sound engineer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes145_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-hughes145-4">[4]</a></sup> Spears traveled to New York with the demo and met with executives from four labels, returning to Kentwood the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes145_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-hughes145-4">[4]</a></sup> Three of the labels rejected her, arguing audiences wanted pop bands such as the <a href="/wiki/Backstreet_Boys" title="Backstreet Boys">Backstreet Boys</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Spice_Girls" title="Spice Girls">Spice Girls</a>, and "there wasn't going to be another <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>, another <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Gibson" title="Debbie Gibson">Debbie Gibson</a>, or another <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiffany_(American_singer)" title="Tiffany (American singer)">Tiffany</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes145_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-hughes145-4">[4]</a></sup> Two weeks later, executives from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JIVE_Records" title="JIVE Records">JIVE Records</a> returned calls to Rudolph.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes145_4-6"><a href="#cite_note-hughes145-4">[4]</a></sup> Senior vice president of <a href="/wiki/Artists_and_repertoire" title="Artists and repertoire">A&amp;R</a> Jeff Fenster stated about Spears's audition that "It's very rare to hear someone that age who can deliver emotional content and commercial appeal. [...] For any artist, the motivation—the 'eye of the tiger'— is extremely important. And Britney had that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs1_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-rs1-5">[5]</a></sup> They appointed her to work with producer Eric Foster White for a month, who reportedly shaped her voice from "lower and less poppy" delivery to "distinctively, unmistakably Britney."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hughes_2005_147_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hughes_2005_147-6">[6]</a></sup> After hearing the recorded material, president <a href="/wiki/Clive_Calder" title="Clive Calder">Clive Calder</a> ordered a full album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hughes_2005_147_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hughes_2005_147-6">[6]</a></sup> Spears had originally envisioned "<a href="/wiki/Sheryl_Crow" title="Sheryl Crow">Sheryl Crow</a> music, but younger more adult contemporary" but felt all right with her label's appointment of producers, since "It made more sense to go pop, because I can dance to it—it's more me." She flew to <a href="/wiki/Cheiron_Studios" title="Cheiron Studios">Cheiron Studios</a> in Stockholm, Sweden, where half of the album was recorded from March to April 1998, with producers <a href="/wiki/Max_Martin" title="Max Martin">Max Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denniz_Pop" title="Denniz Pop">Denniz Pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rami_Yacoub" title="Rami Yacoub">Rami Yacoub</a>, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs1_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-rs1-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsintw_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsintw-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Martin showed Spears and her management a track titled "Hit Me Baby One More Time", which was originally written for American group <a href="/wiki/Backstreet_Boys" title="Backstreet Boys">Backstreet Boys</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%26B" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> group <a href="/wiki/TLC_(group)" title="TLC (group)">TLC</a>; however, when the song was submitted to them, they rejected it. Spears later claimed that she felt excited when she heard it and knew it was going to be a hit record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-especial_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-especial-1">[1]</a></sup> "We at JIVE said, 'This is a ... smash'," revealed the label's A&amp;R executive at the time Steven Lunt;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> however, other executives were concerned that the line "Hit Me" would condone <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a>, later being revised to "...Baby One More Time".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-especial_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-especial-1">[1]</a></sup> Spears recorded her vocals for the song in March 1998 at <a href="/wiki/Cheiron_Studios" title="Cheiron Studios">Cheiron Studios</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stockholm,_Sweden" title="Stockholm, Sweden">Stockholm, Sweden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-liner-9">[9]</a></sup> The singer revealed that she "didn’t do well at all the first day in the studio [recording the song], I was just too nervous. So I went out that night and had some fun. The next day I was completely relaxed and nailed it. You gotta be relaxed singing ‘… Baby One More Time’."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blender_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-blender-10">[10]</a></sup> The track was produced by Denniz Pop, Martin and Rami, and was also <a href="/wiki/Audio_mixing_(recorded_music)" title="Audio mixing (recorded music)">mixed</a> by Martin at Cheiron Studios.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-liner-9">[9]</a></sup> Thomas Lindberg played the guitar, while Johan Carlberg played the bass guitar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-liner-9">[9]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Background_vocals" title="Background vocals">Background vocals</a> were provided by Spears, Martin and <a href="/wiki/Nana_Hedin" title="Nana Hedin">Nana Hedin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-liner-9">[9]</a></sup> Spears also recorded a track called "Autumn Goodbye", written and produced by Eric Foster White, that was released as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B-side" title="B-side">b-side</a> to "...Baby One More Time".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner2_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-liner2-11">[11]</a></sup> The track was recorded in 1998 at 4MW East Studios in <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner2_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-liner2-11">[11]</a></sup> "...Baby One More Time" was released as Spears's debut single on October 23, 1998, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JIVE_Records" title="JIVE Records">JIVE Records</a>, when she was only 16 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The singer has named "...Baby One More Time" as one of her favorite songs from her entire career,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-t4_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-t4-13">[13]</a></sup> naming "<a href="/wiki/Toxic_(song)" title="Toxic (song)">Toxic</a>" and "He About to Lose Me" as the other two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-t4_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-t4-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Like TLC and Backstreet Boys, British boyband <a href="/wiki/Five_(band)" title="Five (band)">Five</a> were almost considered to record the song, according to former Five manager <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a>, who would work with Spears in the <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S._season_2)" title="The X Factor (U.S. season 2)">second season</a> of the American version of <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The X Factor (U.S. TV series)">The X Factor</a></i> in 2012, in his autobiography <i>Sweet Revenge</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="mbox-small-left" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">

</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">

<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
