</table>
<p>"...Baby One More Time" is a <a href="/wiki/Teen_pop" title="Teen pop">teen pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> song that lasts for three minutes and 30 seconds. The song is composed in the <a href="/wiki/Key_(music)" title="Key (music)">key</a> of <a href="/wiki/C_minor" title="C minor">C minor</a> and is set in the <a href="/wiki/Time_signature" title="Time signature">time signature</a> of 4/4 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_time" title="Common time">common time</a> with a moderate <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">tempo</a> of 93 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beats_per_minute" title="Beats per minute">beats per minute</a> (Andante moderato). Songwriting and production is largely based on previous Cheiron productions, most notably <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robyn_Carlsson" title="Robyn Carlsson">Robyn Carlsson</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Show_Me_Love_(Robyn_song)" title="Show Me Love (Robyn song)">Show Me Love</a>" which shows similar song scheme, drum patterns, wah guitars and piano hits. Spears's vocal range spans over two octaves from E♭<sub>3</sub> to the high-tone of G<sub>5</sub>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-notes_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-notes-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The song begins with a three-note motif in the bass range of the piano, an opening that has been compared to many other songs, such as "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>" (1977), "<a href="/wiki/Start_Me_Up" title="Start Me Up">Start Me Up</a>" (1981) and the theme song of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Jaws_(film)" title="Jaws (film)">Jaws</a></i> due to the fact the track "makes its presence known in exactly one second".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blender_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-blender-10">[10]</a></sup> According to magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i>, "...Baby One More Time" is composed by "<a href="/wiki/Wah-wah_(music)" title="Wah-wah (music)">wah-wah</a> guitar lines and <a href="/wiki/Electrocardiography" title="Electrocardiography">EKG</a>-machine bass-slaps".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blender_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-blender-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Claudia Mitchell and Jacqueline Reid-Walsh, authors of <i>Girl Culture: Studying girl culture : a readers' guide</i> (2008), noted the lyrics of the song "gesture toward [Spears] longing for the return of an ex-boyfriend."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Spears said "...Baby One More Time" is a song "every girl can relate to. She regrets it. She wants him back."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsc_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-tsc-18">[18]</a></sup> The lyrics, however, caused controversy in the United States, because the line "Hit me baby one more time" supposedly has <a href="/wiki/Sadomasochism" title="Sadomasochism">sadomasochistic</a> connotations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E2.80.A6Baby_One_More_Time_Album_Review_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E2.80.A6Baby_One_More_Time_Album_Review-19">[19]</a></sup> As a response, the singer said the line "doesn't mean physically hit me. [...] It means just give me a sign, basically. I think it's kind of funny that people would actually think that's what it meant."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsintw_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsintw-7">[7]</a></sup> Contemporary author <a href="/wiki/Ben_Shapiro" title="Ben Shapiro">Ben Shapiro</a> deemed the song's lyrics as suggestive, mostly "Oh baby, baby / The reason I breathe is you / Boy, you got me blinded / Oh pretty baby / There's nothing that I wouldn't do" and "When I'm not with you I lose my mind / Give me a sign / Hit me baby one more time".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg"><img alt="A blond female performer. She is standing on a moving jungle gym, wearing black and white clothes." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2189" data-file-width="3011" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg/220px-Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg/330px-Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg/440px-Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spears and some of her dancers performing "...Baby One More Time" during <a href="/wiki/The_Circus_Starring_Britney_Spears" title="The Circus Starring Britney Spears">The Circus Starring Britney Spears</a>, 2009.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"...Baby One More Time" received generally favorable reviews from contemporary critics, who mostly praised its composition. Marc Oxoby, author of <i>The 1990s</i> (2003), noted the song "was derided as vapid by some critics, yet tapped into the same kind of audience to whom the <a href="/wiki/Spice_Girls" title="Spice Girls">Spice Girls</a> music appealed, young teens and pre-teens."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Amanda Murray of <a href="/wiki/Sputnikmusic" title="Sputnikmusic">Sputnikmusic</a> commented, "["...Baby One More Time" is] well-composed, tightly arranged, and even with Spears's vocal limitations it goes straight for the proverbial pop jugular."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spntk_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-spntk-22">[22]</a></sup> She also said that the song was a highlight in the pop music genre and added, "There is little doubt that '...Baby One More Time' will be long remembered as one of the cornerstones of pop music in general, and it is a strong front-runner as the prototype for the late 90s pop resurgence."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spntk_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-spntk-22">[22]</a></sup> Bill Lamb of <a href="/wiki/About.com" title="About.com">About.com</a> considered "...Baby One More Time" as Spears's best song, saying, "the song is full of hooks and a big mainstream pop sound. The accompanying schoolgirl video caused a sensation, and, when the single hit No. 1, Britney was assured of stardom."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In a list compiled by Sara Anderson of <a href="/wiki/AOL_Radio" title="AOL Radio">AOL Radio</a>, "...Baby One More Time" was ranked sixth in a list of Spears's best songs. She noted the singer "somehow made the school girl outfit and pink pom-pom hair-ties trendy again, worn by every tween in the succeeding years."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Beth Johnson of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> called "...Baby One More Time" a "candy-pop-with-a-<a href="/wiki/Funk" title="Funk">funky</a>-edge smash",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> while Stephen Thomas Erlewine of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic">Allmusic</a> said the song was "ingenious",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Brian Raftery of <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i> called it "a perfectly fine, slickly conceived pop tune. [..] At the time, teen-pop was still a boys’ club, but while the guys were crooning about crushes, Spears was already planning the sleep-over party".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blender_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-blender-10">[10]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> called it "some of the best radio pop of the past decade-plus".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> considered "...Baby One More Time" "incredible",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nme_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-nme-28">[28]</a></sup> commenting that "it's a symphony of teenage lust as fully realised as anything Brian Wilson ever wrote – a truly grand pop song that overwhelms any lingering undercurrent of Lolita paedo-creepiness through the sheer fanatical earnestness of its delivery."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nme_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-nme-28">[28]</a></sup> "...Baby One More Time" won a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Award" title="Teen Choice Award">Teen Choice Award</a> for Single of the Year and an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Award" title="MTV Europe Music Award">MTV Europe Music Award</a> for Best Song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ema_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-ema-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chart_performance">Chart performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Chart performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_2002.jpg"><img alt="Faraway image of a female performer. She is walking through a water screen that is falling from the ceiling. A blue spotlight is on her. She is wearing blue jeans and a plastic cowboy hat. Green laser lights surround the stage." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1101" data-file-width="1079" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Britney_Spears_2002.jpg/220px-Britney_Spears_2002.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Britney_Spears_2002.jpg/330px-Britney_Spears_2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Britney_Spears_2002.jpg/440px-Britney_Spears_2002.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_2002.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The encore performance of "...Baby One More Time" during the <a href="/wiki/Dream_Within_a_Dream_Tour" title="Dream Within a Dream Tour">Dream Within a Dream Tour</a>, with Spears standing in the water screen, 2001.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The song was officially sent to the American radio stations on October 23, 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-especial_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-especial-1">[1]</a></sup> On November 21, 1998, "...Baby One More Time" debuted on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> at number 17 and topped the chart two and a half months later for two consecutive weeks, replacing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%26B" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>-singer <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Have_You_Ever%3F" title="Have You Ever?">Have You Ever?</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hot100feb6_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-hot100feb6-30">[30]</a></sup> Simultaneously, it climbed to number-one on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Singles_Chart" title="Canadian Singles Chart">Canadian Singles Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_charts_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_charts-31">[31]</a></sup> The song reached the top spot of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_100_Singles_Sales" title="Hot 100 Singles Sales">Hot 100 Singles Sales</a> and stayed there for four consecutive weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> This eventually propelled the single to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Platinum_single" title="Platinum single">platinum certification</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAA_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-34">[34]</a></sup> Though not as strong as its sales tallies, "...Baby One More Time" also experienced considerable airplay, becoming her first top ten hit on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_100_Airplay" title="Hot 100 Airplay">Hot 100 Airplay</a>, peaking at number eight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The single also became an all-around hit on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Top_40_radio" title="Top 40 radio">Top 40 radio</a>, going top ten on both the <a href="/wiki/Top_40_Tracks" title="Top 40 Tracks">Top 40 Tracks</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhythmic_Top_40" title="Rhythmic Top 40">Rhythmic Top 40</a>, and to number one for five weeks on the <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40" title="Mainstream Top 40">Mainstream Top 40</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_charts_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_charts-31">[31]</a></sup> It spent 32 weeks on the Hot 100 and ended up at number five on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billboard_magazine" title="Billboard magazine">Billboard magazine</a>'s year-end chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboardhot100_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboardhot100-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Annual_Chart_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Annual_Chart-37">[37]</a></sup> As of June 2012, "...Baby One More Time" has sold 1,412,000 physical singles, with 511,000 paid digital downloads in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-best_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-best-38">[38]</a></sup> It is Spears's best-selling physical single in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-best_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-best-38">[38]</a></sup> "...Baby One More Time" debuted at number 20 on the <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">Australian Singles Chart</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_charts_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA_charts-39">[39]</a></sup> a month later reached number one and stayed there for nine consecutive weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_charts_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA_charts-39">[39]</a></sup> The song eventually became the second <a href="/wiki/List_of_Top_25_singles_for_1999_in_Australia" title="List of Top 25 singles for 1999 in Australia">highest-selling single of the year</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_Annual_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA_Annual-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA-41">[41]</a></sup> only behind <a href="/wiki/Lou_Bega" title="Lou Bega">Lou Bega</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Mambo_No._5" title="Mambo No. 5">Mambo#5</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_Annual_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA_Annual-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA-41">[41]</a></sup> and was certified three-times platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a> for selling over 210,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_Annual_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA_Annual-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_41-2"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA-41">[41]</a></sup> In New Zealand, the single spent four non-consecutive weeks at the top of the charts and after shipping over 15,000 units to retailers the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_New_Zealand" title="Recording Industry Association of New Zealand">Recording Industry Association of New Zealand</a> certified it platinum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIANZ_charts_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIANZ_charts-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIANZ_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIANZ-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The track reached the top spot in every European country in which it charted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French_charts_lescharts_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-French_charts_lescharts-44">[44]</a></sup> "...Baby One More Time" spent two consecutive weeks at number-one on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Singles_Chart" title="French Singles Chart">French Singles Chart</a> and was certified platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Syndicat_National_de_l%27%C3%89dition_Phonographique" title="Syndicat National de l'Édition Phonographique">Syndicat National de l'Édition Phonographique</a> after selling over 500,000 units in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French_charts_lescharts_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-French_charts_lescharts-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNEP_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-SNEP-45">[45]</a></sup> Additionally, the song topped the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_Control_Charts" title="Media Control Charts">German Singles Chart</a> for six consecutive weeks and sold over 750,000 copies, resulting in a three-times gold certification by the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_the_Phonographic_Industry" title="International Federation of the Phonographic Industry">International Federation of the Phonographic Industry</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IFPI_Germany_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-IFPI_Germany-46">[46]</a></sup> In the United Kingdom, according to JIVE Records, the single "…Baby One More Time" sold more than 250,000 copies in a mere three days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Spears broke a first-week sales record for a female act at the time when "...Baby One More Time" sold a total of 460,000 copies in the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">United Kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fastest-selling_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-fastest-selling-48">[48]</a></sup> The single went on to sell over 1.5 million units,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_sales_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK_sales-49">[49]</a></sup> making it the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles_by_year_(UK)" title="List of best-selling singles by year (UK)">highest-selling single of the year</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of best-selling singles in the United Kingdom">32nd best-selling of all-time in Britain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_sales_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK_sales-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_OOC_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK_OOC-50">[50]</a></sup> Eventually, the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> certified it two-times platinum on March 26, 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPI_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-BPI-51">[51]</a></sup> Additionally, "...Baby One More Time" is the fifth best-selling single by a female artist in the country, just behind <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Believe_(Cher_song)" title="Believe (Cher song)">Believe</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_OOC_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK_OOC-50">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/I_Will_Always_Love_You" title="I Will Always Love You">I Will Always Love You</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OCC_quiz_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-OCC_quiz-52">[52]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adele_(singer)" title="Adele (singer)">Adele</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Someone_like_You_(Adele_song)" title="Someone like You (Adele song)">Someone like You</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%A9line_Dion" title="Céline Dion">Céline Dion</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/My_Heart_Will_Go_On" title="My Heart Will Go On">My Heart Will Go On</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OCC_quiz_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-OCC_quiz-52">[52]</a></sup> "...Baby One More Time" is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles" title="List of best-selling singles">best-selling singles of all time</a>, with over 10 million copies sold worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_video">Music video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Music video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_2">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The music video was filmed on August 6, 7 and 8, 1998, and was directed by <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Dick" title="Nigel Dick">Nigel Dick</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-video_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-video-55">[55]</a></sup> After being chosen, Dick received criticism from his colleagues about wanting to work with Spears. He responded saying, "It's a great song. I don't know anything about Britney. I never watched <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mickey_Mouse_Club#1990s_revival.2C_The_All-New_Mickey_Mouse_Club_.28MMC.29" title="The Mickey Mouse Club">The Mickey Mouse Club</a></i>. She seems like a great kid and she's very enthusiastic, but I just love the song. It's just a great song".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsc_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-tsc-18">[18]</a></sup> The video's original setup was in high contrast to what eventually became the final product. The plan was to have the video in a <a href="/wiki/Cartoon" title="Cartoon">cartoon-like</a> environment, in a likely attempt to attract the audience of younger children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-video_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-video-55">[55]</a></sup> Spears was unhappy with this, and argued that she wanted her video to reflect the lives of her fans and wanted to set the video in a school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsc_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-tsc-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-video_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-video-55">[55]</a></sup> Spears pitched this idea to Dick, and further explained she wanted the video to have dance scenes. The original setting was scrapped and replaced with Spears's concept.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsc_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-tsc-18">[18]</a></sup> Dick's original idea for the wardrobe was jeans and a T-shirt, but during the wardrobe fitting Spears decided to change it for a <a href="/wiki/Student" title="Student">schoolgirl</a> outfit. Dick said that "Every piece of wardrobe in the video came from <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a>, and I was told at the time not one piece of clothing in the video cost more than $17. On that level, it's real. That probably, in retrospect, is a part of its charm."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsc_18-4"><a href="#cite_note-tsc-18">[18]</a></sup> The knotted shirt design was Spears's idea, she recollects saying, "The outfits looked kind of dorky, so I was like, 'Let's tie up our shirts and be cute'".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> About the experience of shooting her first music video, Spears said, "It was a wonderful experience. All these people there, working for you. I had my own trailer. It was an amazing experience".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsc_18-5"><a href="#cite_note-tsc-18">[18]</a></sup> The music video was shot at <a href="/wiki/Venice_High_School_(Los_Angeles)" title="Venice High School (Los Angeles)">Venice High School</a>, the same school used to film the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Grease_(film)" title="Grease (film)">Grease</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-video_55-3"><a href="#cite_note-video-55">[55]</a></sup> The video premiered on MTV and other video stations in November 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Synopsis">Synopsis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Synopsis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BabyOneMoreTimeMusicVideo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="171" data-file-width="300" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a0/BabyOneMoreTimeMusicVideo.jpg/220px-BabyOneMoreTimeMusicVideo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a0/BabyOneMoreTimeMusicVideo.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BabyOneMoreTimeMusicVideo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spears wearing the schoolgirl outfit in the song's music video</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The video begins with Spears appearing bored in class at a Catholic high school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-video_55-4"><a href="#cite_note-video-55">[55]</a></sup> Her assistant Felicia Culotta played the role of Spears's teacher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-video_55-5"><a href="#cite_note-video-55">[55]</a></sup> When the bell rings, Spears runs out into the hall and begins a choreographed dance in the corridor. After this, Spears is outside, now adorned in an pink athletic outfit, and seen in a car. Along with a couple of other students, she performs a number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gymnastic" title="Gymnastic">gymnastic</a> moves before heading back inside. She is then sitting on the <a href="/wiki/Bleacher" title="Bleacher">bleachers</a> in the gymnasium watching a basketball game, and she dances in the gymnasium. Her love interest is revealed sitting close to her, played by her real-life cousin Chad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-video_55-6"><a href="#cite_note-video-55">[55]</a></sup> After this short segment, Spears begins her final dance routine and the video ends shortly afterwards, and the bell rings and Spears leaves the gymnasium, revealing that the whole thing had actually just been Spears's <a href="/wiki/Daydream" title="Daydream">daydream</a>. During the very beginning, Spears is seen with her sleeves down. Some people who see the music video may not recognize this, but when the bell rings, the sleeves of the exact same gray-and-white shirt she is wearing are rolled up, even when she gets into singing. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-video_55-7"><a href="#cite_note-video-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The schoolgirl outfit is considered to be one of Spears's iconic looks and is on display<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (April 2016)">vague</span></a></i>]</sup> at the <a href="/wiki/Hard_Rock_Hotel_and_Casino_(Las_Vegas)" title="Hard Rock Hotel and Casino (Las Vegas)">Hard Rock Hotel and Casino</a> in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The ensemble caused controversy among parents associations for showing the <a href="/wiki/Midriff" title="Midriff">midriff</a> of a sixteen-year-old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsc_18-6"><a href="#cite_note-tsc-18">[18]</a></sup> Spears faced the criticism saying, "Me showing my belly? I'm from <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">the South</a>; you're stupid if you don't wear a sports bra [when you] go to dance class, you're going to be sweating your butt off."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsc_18-7"><a href="#cite_note-tsc-18">[18]</a></sup> In 1999, "...Baby One More Time" earned Spears her first three <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award" title="MTV Video Music Award">MTV Video Music Award</a> nominations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vma_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-vma-59">[59]</a></sup> in the categories of <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Pop_Video" title="MTV Video Music Award for Best Pop Video">Best Pop Video</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vma_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-vma-59">[59]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Choreography" title="MTV Video Music Award for Best Choreography">Best Choreography</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vma_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-vma-59">[59]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Female_Video" title="MTV Video Music Award for Best Female Video">Best Female Video</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vma_59-3"><a href="#cite_note-vma-59">[59]</a></sup> In a list compiled by VH1 in 2001, it was listed at number ninety in the best videos of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The video was the first of fourteen of her videos to <a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">retire</a> on MTV's television series <a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">TRL</a>. On its final episode, a three-hour special aired on November 16, 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trlfinale_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-trlfinale-61">[61]</a></sup> "…Baby One More Time" was number one in their final countdown as the most iconic music videos of all time and was the last video to be played on the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trlfinale_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-trlfinale-61">[61]</a></sup> Wesley Yang in his essay "Inside the Box" in <i><a href="/wiki/N%2B1" title="N+1">n+1</a></i>, compared the music video to <a href="/wiki/Britny_Fox" title="Britny Fox">Britny Fox</a>'s "Girlschool" because it featured "a classroom full of Catholic schoolgirls gyrating to the beat in defiance of a stern teacher. [..] But that was a sexist video by a horrible hair metal band that exploited women. Britney Spears was something else—an inflection point in the culture".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The music video is also referenced in the music video of Spears's 2000 single, "<a href="/wiki/Stronger_(Britney_Spears_song)" title="Stronger (Britney Spears song)">Stronger</a>" where Spears sings, "My loneliness ain't killing me no more" - a reference to "...Baby One More Time" where she sings, "My loneliness is killing me." The music video is also referenced in the 2009 single, "<a href="/wiki/If_U_Seek_Amy" title="If U Seek Amy">If U Seek Amy</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bestmtv_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-bestmtv-63">[63]</a></sup> After she comes out of the house dressed as a housewife,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bestmtv_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-bestmtv-63">[63]</a></sup> her daughter is dressed with a similar schoolgirl outfit while wearing pink ribbons in her hair.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bestmtv_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-bestmtv-63">[63]</a></sup> The video was ranked at number four on a list of the ten most controversial music videos in pop by AOL on September 29, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In April 2014, the music video for "...Baby One More Time" reached over 100 million views on VEVO becoming Spears' 5th music video to do so and making it the first 90's video by a female singer to receive a certification.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performances">Live performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Live performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Femme_Fatale_Vancouver_13.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Femme_Fatale_Vancouver_13.jpg/200px-Femme_Fatale_Vancouver_13.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Femme_Fatale_Vancouver_13.jpg/300px-Femme_Fatale_Vancouver_13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Femme_Fatale_Vancouver_13.jpg/400px-Femme_Fatale_Vancouver_13.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Femme_Fatale_Vancouver_13.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spears and some of her dancers performing "...Baby One More Time" during the <a href="/wiki/Femme_Fatale_Tour" title="Femme Fatale Tour">Femme Fatale Tour</a>, 2011.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Spears performed "...Baby One More Time" on several occasions. She performed the song on July 6, 1999, during her appearance at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodstock_1999" title="Woodstock 1999">Woodstock 99</a> festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Woodstock_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Woodstock-65">[65]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Neil_Strauss" title="Neil Strauss">Neil Strauss</a>, from <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, noted that "all the backing music was on tape, and most of the vocals were recorded, with Ms. Spears just reinforcing selected words in choruses and singing an occasional snippet of a verse".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Woodstock_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-Woodstock-65">[65]</a></sup> It was also performed at the <a href="/wiki/1999_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="1999 MTV Video Music Awards">1999 MTV Video Music Awards</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> after a classroom <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/roll_call" title="wikt:roll call">roll call</a> ended, Spears appeared on the stage and began performing the song. Halfway through, she was joined by <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a> and the members of <a href="/wiki/NSYNC" title="NSYNC">NSYNC</a> for a dance routine. Afterwards, the band performed their hit "<a href="/wiki/Tearin%27_Up_My_Heart" title="Tearin' Up My Heart">Tearin' Up My Heart</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The song was also performed at the <a href="/wiki/1999_MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" title="1999 MTV Europe Music Awards">1999 MTV Europe Music Awards</a>, along with "<a href="/wiki/(You_Drive_Me)_Crazy" title="(You Drive Me) Crazy">(You Drive Me) Crazy</a>", the 1999 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards" title="Billboard Music Awards">Billboard Music Awards</a>, the 1999 <a href="/wiki/Smash_Hits_Poll_Winners_Party" title="Smash Hits Poll Winners Party">Smash Hits Poll Winners Party</a>, the Christmas Day edition of <a href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops" title="Top of the Pops">Top of the Pops</a> and the Greenwich Millennium concert on 31 December 1999, she also performed it with broadcasters <a href="/wiki/David_Dimbleby" title="David Dimbleby">David Dimbleby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Buerk" title="Michael Buerk">Michael Buerk</a> on <a href="/wiki/2000_Today" title="2000 Today">2000 Today</a>. Spears performed the song in a medley with "<a href="/wiki/From_the_Bottom_of_My_Broken_Heart" title="From the Bottom of My Broken Heart">From the Bottom of My Broken Heart</a>" at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/42nd_Grammy_Awards" title="42nd Grammy Awards">42nd Grammy Awards</a>. Spears was wearing a turtleneck and a full tulle skirt at the beginning of the performance, while dancers surrounded her with enormous <a href="/wiki/Hand_fan" title="Hand fan">hand fans</a>. After singing a shortened version of the song, she then took a few moments to shuffle into a form-fitting red rhinestone outfit (with side cutouts) and emerged onto a stage to perform "...Baby One More Time." Spears was also criticized of lipsynching the song during her performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvgrammy_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvgrammy-68">[68]</a></sup> Later, in 2003, Spears performed the song in a remixed form at <i>Britney Spears: In the Zone</i>, a concert special that aired in <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> on November 17, 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dispatch_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-dispatch-69">[69]</a></sup> "...Baby One More Time" was also performed at the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League_Kickoff_game" title="National Football League Kickoff game">2003 NFL Kickoff Live</a> on September 4, 2003, at the <a href="/wiki/National_Mall" title="National Mall">National Mall</a>, in a medley with "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_a_Slave_4_U" title="I'm a Slave 4 U">I'm a Slave 4 U</a>" (2001), which included pyrotechnics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coy_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-coy-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auction_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-auction-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nfl_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-nfl-72">[72]</a></sup> She sported shoulder-length blond hair and was dressed in black football pants, a black-and-white referee halter top and boots from <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-post-73">[73]</a></sup> Her outfit was later auctioned off to benefit the Britney Spears Foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auction_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-auction-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>"...Baby One More Time" has been performed in seven of Spears's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concert_tour" title="Concert tour">concert tours</a> since its release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfc_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-sfc-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitch_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-pitch-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livedesign_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-livedesign-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvreview_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvreview-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seattlereview_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-seattlereview-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mms_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-mms-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbcp_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-msnbcp-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usat_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-usat-81">[81]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_Tour" title="...Baby One More Time Tour">...Baby One More Time Tour</a>, the encore consisted of a performance of the song,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfc_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-sfc-74">[74]</a></sup> in which Spears wore a black bra under pink <a href="/wiki/Halter" title="Halter">halter</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfc_74-2"><a href="#cite_note-sfc-74">[74]</a></sup> a pink sequined plaid mini-skirt,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfc_74-3"><a href="#cite_note-sfc-74">[74]</a></sup> and black <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thigh-high_stockings" title="Thigh-high stockings">thigh-high stockings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfc_74-4"><a href="#cite_note-sfc-74">[74]</a></sup> On 2000s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oops!..._I_Did_It_Again_World_Tour" title="Oops!... I Did It Again World Tour">Oops!... I Did It Again World Tour</a>, "...Baby One More Time" was performed after a dance interlude in which the dancers showed their individual moves while their names appeared on the screens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitch_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-pitch-75">[75]</a></sup> Spears took the stage in a conservative schoolgirl outfit to perform the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitch_75-2"><a href="#cite_note-pitch-75">[75]</a></sup> She ripped it off halfway through the song to reveal a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cheerleader" title="Cheerleader">cheerleader</a> ensemble.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitch_75-3"><a href="#cite_note-pitch-75">[75]</a></sup> The song was also the encore of 2001's <a href="/wiki/Dream_Within_a_Dream_Tour" title="Dream Within a Dream Tour">Dream Within a Dream Tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livedesign_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-livedesign-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvreview_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtvreview-77">[77]</a></sup> It began with a giant projection of a hologram of Spears onto a water screen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livedesign_76-2"><a href="#cite_note-livedesign-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvreview_77-2"><a href="#cite_note-mtvreview-77">[77]</a></sup> The projection gradually shrunk until Spears rose from the stage while wearing a plastic cowboy hat, blue hip-huggers, and a matching bra top.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livedesign_76-3"><a href="#cite_note-livedesign-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvreview_77-3"><a href="#cite_note-mtvreview-77">[77]</a></sup> She began performing "...Baby One More Time" in a ballad version until reaching the end of the runway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livedesign_76-4"><a href="#cite_note-livedesign-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvreview_77-4"><a href="#cite_note-mtvreview-77">[77]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pyrotechnics" title="Pyrotechnics">Pyrotechnics</a> surrounded the stage while the song changed to a more uptempo version with elements of <a href="/wiki/Techno" title="Techno">techno</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livedesign_76-5"><a href="#cite_note-livedesign-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvreview_77-5"><a href="#cite_note-mtvreview-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>On <a href="/wiki/The_Onyx_Hotel_Tour" title="The Onyx Hotel Tour">The Onyx Hotel Tour</a>, after performing "<a href="/wiki/In_the_Zone" title="In the Zone">Showdown</a>", a video interlude followed featuring Spears and her friends outside a club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seattlereview_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-seattlereview-78">[78]</a></sup> While she was leaving, she noticed a woman dressed in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1930%E2%80%9345_in_fashion" title="1930–45 in fashion">1930s fashion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seattlereview_78-2"><a href="#cite_note-seattlereview-78">[78]</a></sup> She followed her and the woman asked Spears to enter the "Mystic Lounge".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seattlereview_78-3"><a href="#cite_note-seattlereview-78">[78]</a></sup> Spears reappeared wearing a corset to perform "…Baby One More Time" along with "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oops!...I_Did_It_Again_(song)" title="Oops!...I Did It Again (song)">Oops!...I Did It Again</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/(You_Drive_Me)_Crazy" title="(You Drive Me) Crazy">(You Drive Me) Crazy</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seattlereview_78-4"><a href="#cite_note-seattlereview-78">[78]</a></sup> All of the three were reworked for the show with elements of <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rehearsal_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-rehearsal-82">[82]</a></sup> "...Baby One More Time" was also performed on the promotional tour made on some <a href="/wiki/House_of_Blues" title="House of Blues">House of Blues</a> locations, called <a href="/wiki/The_M%2BM%27s_Tour" title="The M+M's Tour">The M+M's Tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mms_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-mms-79">[79]</a></sup> The show started with Spears singing a short version of the song dressed in a white <a href="/wiki/Go-go_boot" title="Go-go boot">go-go boots</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mms_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-mms-79">[79]</a></sup> a white <a href="/wiki/Miniskirt" title="Miniskirt">miniskirt</a> and a sparkling pink <a href="/wiki/Bikini" title="Bikini">bikini</a> top.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mms_79-3"><a href="#cite_note-mms-79">[79]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/The_Circus_Starring_Britney_Spears" title="The Circus Starring Britney Spears">The Circus Starring Britney Spears</a>, the song made into the Electro Circ act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbcp_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-msnbcp-80">[80]</a></sup> It was the final song of the act,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usat_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-usat-81">[81]</a></sup> performed after "<a href="/wiki/Toxic_(song)" title="Toxic (song)">Toxic</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usat_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-usat-81">[81]</a></sup> The performance consisted on Spears and her dancers performing a remix of the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usat_81-3"><a href="#cite_note-usat-81">[81]</a></sup> On 2011's <a href="/wiki/Femme_Fatale_Tour" title="Femme Fatale Tour">Femme Fatale Tour</a>, "...Baby One More Time" was performed in a medley with the remix of <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/S%26M_(song)" title="S&amp;M (song)">S&amp;M</a>" (2010).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> On Spears' current residency show <a href="/wiki/Britney:_Piece_of_Me" title="Britney: Piece of Me">Britney: Piece of Me</a> in Las Vegas, the song was included on its setlist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BillboardReview_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-BillboardReview-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cover_versions.2C_samples_and_usage_in_media">Cover versions, samples and usage in media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Cover versions, samples and usage in media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glee_cast.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Glee_cast.jpg/220px-Glee_cast.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Glee_cast.jpg/330px-Glee_cast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Glee_cast.jpg/440px-Glee_cast.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Glee_cast.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lea_Michele" title="Lea Michele">Lea Michele</a> from the cast of <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i> covered the song in the episode "<a href="/wiki/Britney/Brittany" title="Britney/Brittany">Britney/Brittany</a>". The episode featured an appearance made by Spears herself.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"…Baby One More Time" has been <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">covered</a> on numerous occasions. One of the earliest live covers of the song was by the Scottish band <a href="/wiki/Travis_(band)" title="Travis (band)">Travis</a>, recorded during one of their concerts at "The Bay Tavern" in <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood%27s_Bay" title="Robin Hood's Bay">Robin Hood's Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire" title="North Yorkshire">North Yorkshire</a>, England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-85">[85]</a></sup> The song was later included in the release of their 1999 single, "<a href="/wiki/Turn_(Travis_song)" title="Turn (Travis song)">Turn</a>". Lead singer Francis Healey said, "We did it for a laugh the first time. [..] And as we played it, the irony slipped from my smile. It's a very well-crafted song. It [has] that magic thing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blender_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-blender-10">[10]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> said this cover showed a new and more "dark" side of the band, commenting "slowed down to a mournful crawl, it was amazing how ominous the couplet "This loneliness is killing me / Hit me, baby, one more time" sounded".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-85">[85]</a></sup> PopWreckoning.com called it "perhaps the most well done cover of Britney's catalyst to eternal fame".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pw_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-pw-86">[86]</a></sup> Spears heard their version while shopping in a mall and said, "It was so weird. I liked it though, I thought it was cool. It was a very different vibe from what I did".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nme2000_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-nme2000-87">[87]</a></sup> In July 2005, <a href="/wiki/The_Dresden_Dolls" title="The Dresden Dolls">The Dresden Dolls</a> performed a cover during their summer concerts while opening for <a href="/wiki/Panic!_at_the_Disco" title="Panic! at the Disco">Panic! at the Disco</a>. On July 18, 2006, frontman <a href="/wiki/Brendon_Urie" title="Brendon Urie">Brendon Urie</a> joined the band to perform the song in <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, Pennsylvania. PopWreckoning.com said the cover was "a strange twist to this pop ditty. It's obviously darker and actually tortured as opposed to Britney's school girl despair".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pw_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-pw-86">[86]</a></sup> The song was featured in a scene in <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>'s directorial debut <i><a href="/wiki/Filth_and_Wisdom" title="Filth and Wisdom">Filth and Wisdom</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> On November 29, 2008, the same day Spears performed "<a href="/wiki/Womanizer_(song)" title="Womanizer (song)">Womanizer</a>" on <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK_series_5)" title="The X Factor (UK series 5)">The X Factor</a></i>, contestants <a href="/wiki/JLS" title="JLS">JLS</a> performed a cover of the song that was deemed "lame" by judge <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mj_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-mj-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 13, 2009, <a href="/wiki/Tori_Amos" title="Tori Amos">Tori Amos</a> covered the song live during her <a href="/wiki/Sinful_Attraction_Tour" title="Sinful Attraction Tour">Sinful Attraction Tour</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Theatre_(Oakland,_California)" title="Paramount Theatre (Oakland, California)">Paramount Theatre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">Oakland, California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tori_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-tori-90">[90]</a></sup> On October 15, 2009, <a href="/wiki/Kris_Allen" title="Kris Allen">Kris Allen</a> covered the song for the first time at a concert in <a href="/wiki/Seton_High_School_(Cincinnati,_Ohio)" title="Seton High School (Cincinnati, Ohio)">Seton High School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a>, Ohio. His rendition received positive reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-ew-91">[91]</a></sup> An excerpt was used in <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">CGI</a>-animated <a href="/wiki/Comedy_film" title="Comedy film">comedy film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Robots_(2005_film)" title="Robots (2005 film)">Robots</a></i>, but was not included on the soundtrack album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Swedish humorist heavy metal band <a href="/wiki/Black_Ingvars" title="Black Ingvars">Black Ingvars</a> covered the song for their 2000 album <i>Kids Superhits</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amazon_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-amazon-93">[93]</a></sup> The same year, British death metal cover band <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ten_Masked_Men&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ten Masked Men (page does not exist)">Ten Masked Men</a> included a rendition of the song on their <i><a href="/wiki/Return_of_the_Ten_Masked_Men" title="Return of the Ten Masked Men">Return of the Ten Masked Men</a></i> album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nmetmk_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-nmetmk-94">[94]</a></sup> A cover by <a href="/wiki/Ahmet_Zappa" title="Ahmet Zappa">Ahmet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dweezil_Zappa" title="Dweezil Zappa">Dweezil Zappa</a> was featured in the soundtrack of the 2000 film <i><a href="/wiki/Ready_to_Rumble" title="Ready to Rumble">Ready to Rumble</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtr_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-rtr-95">[95]</a></sup> In 2003, the song was covered by American pop punk band <a href="/wiki/Bowling_for_Soup" title="Bowling for Soup">Bowling for Soup</a> for the soundtrack of the remake film <i><a href="/wiki/Freaky_Friday_(2003_film)" title="Freaky Friday (2003 film)">Freaky Friday</a></i> and commented that their version was "really, really, dark and really rock, [..] not the kind of 'pop'-py stuff that we usually do."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bfs_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-bfs-96">[96]</a></sup> In 2005, power pop band <a href="/wiki/Fountains_of_Wayne" title="Fountains of Wayne">Fountains of Wayne</a> covered the song for their compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/Out-of-State_Plates" title="Out-of-State Plates">Out-of-State Plates</a></i>. Robert Christgau of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i> highlighted their rendition saying the song is "as redolent and fetching as any of [Fountains of Wayne]'s peaks".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vv_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-vv-97">[97]</a></sup> Japanese pop singer <a href="/wiki/Shiori_Takei" title="Shiori Takei">Shiori Takei</a> covered the song of her 2005 album <i>The Note of My Nineteen Years</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, a <a href="/wiki/Lounge_music" title="Lounge music">lounge music</a> style cover of the song by Trombo Combo was included on their covers album <i>Trombo Combo: Swedish Sound Deluxe</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cdu_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-cdu-99">[99]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Hi-NRG" title="Hi-NRG">hi-NRG</a>-<a href="/wiki/Eurodance" title="Eurodance">eurodance</a> cover by Jayne Montgomery was released through <a href="/wiki/Almighty_Records" title="Almighty Records">Almighty Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> In the 2009 compilation <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punk_Goes_Pop_2" title="Punk Goes Pop 2">Punk Goes Pop 2</a></i>, a cover of the song by metalcore band <a href="/wiki/August_Burns_Red" title="August Burns Red">August Burns Red</a> was included along with a cover of "<a href="/wiki/Toxic_(song)" title="Toxic (song)">Toxic</a>" by <a href="/wiki/A_Static_Lullaby" title="A Static Lullaby">A Static Lullaby</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atp_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-atp-102">[102]</a></sup> Music duo <a href="/wiki/Doll_Factory" title="Doll Factory">Doll Factory</a> included a cover of the song as a bonus track on later printings of their album <i>Weightless</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Dallman" title="Christopher Dallman">Christopher Dallman</a> released an <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> titled <i><a href="/wiki/Sad_Britney" title="Sad Britney">Sad Britney</a></i> that includes a cover of the song along with covers of "Toxic", "<a href="/wiki/Gimme_More" title="Gimme More">Gimme More</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Radar_(song)" title="Radar (song)">Radar</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chrisdal_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-chrisdal-104">[104]</a></sup> The song has also been covered by Brainshake, Intwine, Kevorkian, P.T. Grimm and the Dead Puppies, <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Owen_Youngs" title="Jenny Owen Youngs">Jenny Owen Youngs</a>, Neil Sahgal and Annie Bethancourt, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pw_86-2"><a href="#cite_note-pw-86">[86]</a></sup> In the 2010 <i>Glee</i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Britney/Brittany" title="Britney/Brittany">Britney/Brittany</a>", the character of <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Berry" title="Rachel Berry">Rachel Berry</a>, played by <a href="/wiki/Lea_Michele" title="Lea Michele">Lea Michele</a>, covered the song using similar outfits to the ones of the music video. Spears also made a cameo, taking the teacher's role, previously played by Cullota.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Darren_Criss" title="Darren Criss">Darren Criss</a> also of <i>Glee</i> performed a mash-up of "...Baby One More Time" with "<a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCr_Elise" title="Für Elise">Für Elise</a>" on <i>Sing Out, Raise Hope</i> for The Trevor Project and the Elizabeth Glaser Pediatric AIDS Foundation in December 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In 2012, British singer <a href="/wiki/Ed_Sheeran" title="Ed Sheeran">Ed Sheeran</a> performed an acoustic version of the song NOW 100.5 FM.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> A year later he covered it on <i>The Elvis Duran Z100 Morning Show</i> and added a rap verse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The song is sung by actresses <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanessa_Hudgens" title="Vanessa Hudgens">Vanessa Hudgens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Benson" title="Ashley Benson">Ashley Benson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Korine" title="Rachel Korine">Rachel Korine</a> in <a href="/wiki/Harmony_Korine" title="Harmony Korine">Harmony Korine</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/Spring_Breakers" title="Spring Breakers">Spring Breakers</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hw1_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-hw1-109">[109]</a></sup> Swedish singer <a href="/wiki/Tove_Styrke" title="Tove Styrke">Tove Styrke</a> released a cover of the song on July 24, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BritneyPOM19.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3064" data-file-width="2329" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/BritneyPOM19.jpg/170px-BritneyPOM19.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/BritneyPOM19.jpg/255px-BritneyPOM19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/BritneyPOM19.jpg/340px-BritneyPOM19.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BritneyPOM19.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Britney performing the track during her Las Vegas residency show, <a href="/wiki/Britney:_Piece_of_Me" title="Britney: Piece of Me">Britney: Piece of Me</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"…Baby One More Time" was listed at number twenty five in the greatest pop songs since 1963, in a list compiled by <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> and MTV in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i> listed it at number two in The 500 Greatest Songs Since You Were Born.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blender_10-5"><a href="#cite_note-blender-10">[10]</a></sup> The song was also listed as the 2nd best song of the 1990s by <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> and in a listing compiled in 2003, ranked at number one in 100 Best Songs of the Past 25 Years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Bill Lamb of About.com ranked "...Baby One More Time" at number one on a compiled list with the Top 40 Pop Songs Of All Time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The music video was voted the third most influential promo in the history of pop music on a poll held by <a href="/wiki/Jam!" title="Jam!">Jam!</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> "…Baby One More Time" is also one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles" title="List of best-selling singles">best-selling singles of all time</a>, with over 9 million copies sold,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> and also earned Spears's first nomination for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grammy_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-grammy-117">[117]</a></sup> In April 2005, the British TV network <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> aired a short series called <i><a href="/wiki/Hit_Me,_Baby,_One_More_Time_(TV_series)" title="Hit Me, Baby, One More Time (TV series)">Hit Me, Baby, One More Time</a></i> hosted by <a href="/wiki/Vernon_Kay" title="Vernon Kay">Vernon Kay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb2_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-imdb2-118">[118]</a></sup> The show pitted <a href="/wiki/One-hit_wonder" title="One-hit wonder">one-hit wonders</a> who generally had their moments of fame in the 1980s against each other to play their own hits and a currently popular cover song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb2_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-imdb2-118">[118]</a></sup> The favorites were chosen by audience voting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb2_118-2"><a href="#cite_note-imdb2-118">[118]</a></sup> The American version of the show also aired on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> later in the year, and it was also hosted by Kay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-imdb-119">[119]</a></sup> In the 2012 poll created by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Official_Chart_Company" title="The Official Chart Company">The Official Chart Company</a> and <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> to discover <a href="/wiki/The_Nation%27s_Favourite" title="The Nation's Favourite">The Nation's Favourite Number 1 Single</a> of all-time, "…Baby One More Time" was listed as the seventh favorite song by <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">the United Kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>Spears became an international <a href="/wiki/Pop_icon" title="Pop icon">pop culture icon</a> immediately after launching her recording career. <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine wrote: "One of the most controversial and successful female vocalists of the 21st century," she "spearheaded the rise of post-millennial teen pop ... Spears early on cultivated a mixture of innocence and experience that broke the bank".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Barbara Ellen of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> has reported: "Spears is famously one of the 'oldest' teenagers pop has ever produced, almost middle aged in terms of focus and determination. Many 19-year-olds haven't even started working by that age, whereas Britney, a former Mouseketeer, was that most unusual and volatile of American phenomena — a child with a full-time career. While other little girls were putting posters on their walls, Britney was wanting to be the poster on the wall. Whereas other children develop at their own pace, Britney was developing at a pace set by the ferociously competitive American entertainment industry".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>Scott Plagenhoef of Pitchfork noted "songs like <a href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)" title="Nirvana (band)">Nirvana</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Smells_Like_Teen_Spirit" title="Smells Like Teen Spirit">Smells Like Teen Spirit</a>", <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Nuthin%27_but_a_%27G%27_Thang" title="Nuthin' but a 'G' Thang">Nothing But a G Thang</a>", and Britney Spears's "...Baby One More Time" altered the landscape of pop culture so quickly in large part because they were delivered to all corners of the U.S. simultaneously by MTV. [...] MTV's ability to place a song and musician into the pop music conversation was unparalleled at the time, and by the end of the decade that meant absurd levels of both financial and creative commitment to music videos."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a> writer Evan Sawdey commented that Spears's concept for the music video of the song was the one responsible for her immediate success, saying that, as a result, the singer "scored a massive No. 1 single, inadvertently started the late '90s teen pop boom, and created a public persona for herself that was simultaneously kid-friendly and pure male fantasy. Her videos got played on both MTV and the <a href="/wiki/Disney_Channel" title="Disney Channel">Disney Channel</a> at the same time, showing just how well Spears (and her armies of PR handlers) managed to walk that fine line between family-friendly pop idol and unabashed sex object."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Credits_and_personnel">Credits and personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Credits and personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Credits for "...Baby One More Time" and "Autumn Goodbye" are taken from the single's liner notes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-liner-9">[9]</a></sup></p>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">1952–1969</th>

<li>1957: "<a href="/wiki/Diana_(Paul_Anka_song)" title="Diana (Paul Anka song)">Diana</a>" – <a href="/wiki/Paul_Anka" title="Paul Anka">Paul Anka</a></li>
<li>1958: "<a href="/wiki/Jailhouse_Rock_(song)" title="Jailhouse Rock (song)">Jailhouse Rock</a>" – <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a></li>
<li>1959: "<a href="/wiki/Living_Doll_(song)" title="Living Doll (song)">Living Doll</a>" – <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Richard" title="Cliff Richard">Cliff Richard</a></li>
<li>1960: "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Now_or_Never_(song)" title="It's Now or Never (song)">It's Now or Never</a>" – <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a></li>

<li>1962: "<a href="/wiki/I_Remember_You_(1941_song)" title="I Remember You (1941 song)">I Remember You</a>" – <a href="/wiki/Frank_Ifield" title="Frank Ifield">Frank Ifield</a></li>
<li>1963: "<a href="/wiki/She_Loves_You" title="She Loves You">She Loves You</a>" – <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a></li>
<li>1964: "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Buy_Me_Love" title="Can't Buy Me Love">Can't Buy Me Love</a>" – <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a></li>
<li>1965: "<a href="/wiki/Tears_(Ken_Dodd_song)" title="Tears (Ken Dodd song)">Tears</a>" – <a href="/wiki/Ken_Dodd" title="Ken Dodd">Ken Dodd</a></li>

<li>1967: "<a href="/wiki/Release_Me_(1946_song)" title="Release Me (1946 song)">Release Me</a>" – <a href="/wiki/Engelbert_Humperdinck_(singer)" title="Engelbert Humperdinck (singer)">Engelbert Humperdinck</a></li>
<li>1968: "<a href="/wiki/Hey_Jude" title="Hey Jude">Hey Jude</a>" – <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a></li>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">1970–1989</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-even hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>

<li>1973: "<a href="/wiki/Tie_a_Yellow_Ribbon_Round_the_Ole_Oak_Tree" title="Tie a Yellow Ribbon Round the Ole Oak Tree">Tie a Yellow Ribbon Round the Ole Oak Tree</a>" – <a href="/wiki/Tony_Orlando" title="Tony Orlando">Tony Orlando</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Orlando_and_Dawn" title="Tony Orlando and Dawn">Dawn</a></li>

<li>1975: "<a href="/wiki/Bye,_Bye,_Baby_(Baby_Goodbye)" title="Bye, Bye, Baby (Baby Goodbye)">Bye Bye Baby</a>" – <a href="/wiki/Bay_City_Rollers" title="Bay City Rollers">Bay City Rollers</a></li>
